Now let me also think about the `CertificateChain` field. Looking at the AWS docs for ImportCertificate:

- **Certificate**: The certificate to import. (base64 encoded)
- **PrivateKey**: The private key that matches the public key in the certificate. (base64 encoded)
- **CertificateChain**: The PEM encoded certificate chain. (base64 encoded)

So yes, all three should be base64-decoded. My code handles all three.

Now, let me also think about edge cases for the `decodeBlob` method:
- Null: returns null ✓
- Empty: returns empty ✓
- Starts with `-----BEGIN`: returns as-is (raw PEM) ✓
- Base64 encoded: decodes and returns ✓
- Invalid base64: falls back to returning as-is ✓
- Base64 that decodes to non-PEM: returns as-is (safety check) ✓

Wait, there's a subtle issue. What if a user sends the PEM with `\n` escape sequences in JSON? Like:
```
{"Certificate": "-----BEGIN CERTIFICATE-----\nMIIB...\n-----END CERTIFICATE-----\n"}
```

When Jackson parses this, the `\n` becomes actual newlines, so the Java string would be:
```
-----BEGIN CERTIFICATE-----
MIIB...
-----END CERTIFICATE-----

```

This starts with `-----BEGIN`, so it will be returned as-is. Then `CertificateGenerator.parseCertificate` will parse it correctly. Good.

But what about the test case in `AcmImportExportTest.java` line 58:
```java
String certJson = validTestCertificate.replace("\n", "\\n");
```

Here, `validTestCertificate` is a Java string containing actual newlines. The `.replace("\n", "\\n")` replaces actual newlines with the literal two characters `\n` (backslash + n). When this is placed in the JSON body, Jackson will parse `\\n` as `\n` (actual newline). So the Java string will have actual newlines and start with `-----BEGIN`. Good.

   324	    public Certificate importCertificate(String certificatePem, String privateKeyPem, String chainPem,
   325	                                          String existingArn, Map<String, String> tags, String region) {
   326	        logSecurityWarningOnce();
   327	        // Parse and validate certificate
   328	        X509Certificate x509Cert;
   329	        try {
   330	            x509Cert = certificateGenerator.parseCertificate(certificatePem);
   331	            certificateGenerator.validateCertificate(x509Cert);
   332	        } catch (Exception e) {
   333	            throw new AwsException("ValidationException", "Invalid certificate: " + e.getMessage(), 400);
   334	        }
   335	
   336	        // Parse and validate private key
   337	        try {
   338	            certificateGenerator.parsePrivateKey(privateKeyPem);
   339	        } catch (Exception e) {
   340	            throw new AwsException("ValidationException", "Invalid private key: " + e.getMessage(), 400);
   341	        }
   342	
   343	        if (tags != null) {
   344	            validateTags(tags);
   345	        }
   346	
   347	        String certId;
   348	        String arn;
   349	
   350	        if (existingArn != null && !existingArn.isEmpty()) {
   351	            // Re-import
   352	            Certificate existing = getCertificateByArn(existingArn, region);
   353	            certId = existing.extractCertificateId();
   354	            arn = existingArn;
   355	        } else {
   356	            certId = UUID.randomUUID().toString();
   357	            arn = buildCertificateArn(region, certId);
   358	        }
   359	
   360	        Instant now = Instant.now();
   361	        KeyAlgorithm keyAlg = certificateGenerator.detectKeyAlgorithm(x509Cert.getPublicKey());
   362	
   363	        Certificate cert = new Certificate();
   364	        cert.setArn(arn);
   365	        cert.setDomainName(extractCommonName(x509Cert));
   366	        cert.setStatus(CertificateStatus.ISSUED);
   367	        cert.setType(CertificateType.IMPORTED);
   368	        cert.setCreatedAt(existingArn == null ? now : null);
   369	        cert.setImportedAt(now);
   370	        cert.setIssuedAt(now);
   371	        cert.setNotBefore(x509Cert.getNotBefore().toInstant());
   372	        cert.setNotAfter(x509Cert.getNotAfter().toInstant());
   373	        cert.setSerial(x509Cert.getSerialNumber().toString());
   374	        cert.setSubject(x509Cert.getSubjectX500Principal().getName());
   375	        cert.setIssuer(x509Cert.getIssuerX500Principal().getName());
   376	        cert.setKeyAlgorithm(keyAlg);
   377	        cert.setSignatureAlgorithm(x509Cert.getSigAlgName());
   378	        cert.setCertificateBody(certificatePem);
   379	        cert.setPrivateKey(privateKeyPem);
   380	        cert.setCertificateChain(chainPem);
   381	        cert.setTags(tags != null ? new HashMap<>(tags) : new HashMap<>());
   382	
   383	        String storageKey = regionKey(region, certId);
   384	        store.put(storageKey, cert);
   385	
   386	        LOG.infov("Imported certificate: {0}", arn);
   387	        return cert;
   388	    }

   390	    // ============ ExportCertificate ============
   391	
   392	    public Certificate exportCertificate(String certificateArn, String passphraseBase64, String region) {
   393	        Certificate cert = getCertificateByArn(certificateArn, region);
   394	
   395	        if (!cert.canExport()) {
   396	            throw new AwsException("ValidationException",
   397	                "Certificate is not PRIVATE type and Export is not ENABLED", 400);
   398	        }
   399	
   400	        String passphrase;
   401	        try {
   402	            passphrase = new String(Base64.getDecoder().decode(passphraseBase64));
   403	        } catch (Exception e) {
   404	            throw new AwsException("ValidationException", "Invalid passphrase encoding", 400);
   405	        }
   406	
   407	        if (passphrase.length() < 4) {
   408	            throw new AwsException("ValidationException", "Passphrase must be at least 4 characters", 400);
   409	        }
   410	
   411	        // Encrypt the private key
   412	        String encryptedKey = certificateGenerator.encryptPrivateKey(cert.getPrivateKey(), passphrase);
   413	
   414	        // Return certificate with encrypted private key
   415	        Certificate exportCert = new Certificate();
   416	        exportCert.setCertificateBody(cert.getCertificateBody());
   417	        exportCert.setCertificateChain(cert.getCertificateChain());
   418	        exportCert.setPrivateKey(encryptedKey);
   419	        return exportCert;
   420	    }

   635	    private String extractCommonName(X509Certificate cert) {
   636	        String dn = cert.getSubjectX500Principal().getName();
   637	        return Arrays.stream(dn.split(","))
   638	            .map(String::trim)
   639	            .filter(s -> s.startsWith("CN="))
   640	            .findFirst()
   641	            .map(s -> s.substring(3))
   642	            .orElse(dn);
   643	    }

   137	    private Response handleImportCertificate(JsonNode request, String region) {
   138	        // AWS JSON 1.1 protocol: Certificate, PrivateKey, and CertificateChain are base64-encoded
   139	        String certificate = decodeBlob(request.path("Certificate").asText(), "Certificate");
   140	        String privateKey = decodeBlob(request.path("PrivateKey").asText(), "PrivateKey");
   141	        String chain = request.path("CertificateChain").asText(null);
   142	        if (chain != null) {
   143	            chain = decodeBlob(chain, "CertificateChain");
   144	        }
   145	        String existingArn = request.path("CertificateArn").asText(null);
   146	        Map<String, String> tags = parseTags(request.path("Tags"));
   147	
   148	        Certificate cert = service.importCertificate(certificate, privateKey, chain, existingArn, tags, region);
   149	
   150	        ObjectNode response = objectMapper.createObjectNode();
   151	        response.put("CertificateArn", cert.getArn());
   152	        return Response.ok(response).build();
   153	    }
   154	
   155	    /**
   156	     * Decodes a base64-encoded blob field, with fallback for plain-text PEM.
   157	     *
   158	     * <p>The AWS JSON 1.1 protocol specifies that binary blob fields (like Certificate,
   159	     * PrivateKey, CertificateChain) are base64-encoded. However, some SDKs or direct HTTP
   160	     * calls may send the raw PEM text. This method detects base64 encoding and decodes
   161	     * accordingly.</p>
   162	     */
   163	    private String decodeBlob(String value, String fieldName) {
   164	        if (value == null || value.isEmpty()) {
   165	            return value;
   166	        }
   167	        // If the value looks like PEM (starts with "-----BEGIN"), it's already plain text
   168	        if (value.startsWith("-----BEGIN")) {
   169	            return value;
   170	        }
   171	        // Otherwise, try to base64-decode it.
   172	        // Use MIME decoder to handle possible whitespace/newlines in the base64 string.
   173	        try {
   174	            byte[] decoded = java.util.Base64.getMimeDecoder().decode(value);
   175	            String result = new String(decoded, java.nio.charset.StandardCharsets.UTF_8);
   176	            // Verify the decoded result is valid PEM text
   177	            if (result.startsWith("-----BEGIN")) {
   178	                return result;
   179	            }
   180	            // If decoded but doesn't look like PEM, return original (might be a different encoding)
   181	            return value;
   182	        } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) {
   183	            // Not valid base64 - return as-is (it might be plain text with escaped newlines)
   184	            return value;
   185	        }
   186	    }

- It doesn't start with `-----BEGIN`
- Try base64 decode: `Base64.getMimeDecoder().decode("not-a-valid-certificate")` - this will throw `IllegalArgumentException` because it's not valid base64
- Catch, return as-is
- Then `parseCertificate("not-a-valid-certificate")` will fail with "Invalid certificate PEM format"
- The service catches this and throws `AwsException` with "Invalid certificate: ..."
- The handler returns 400

This matches the expected test behavior at line 292-307: `importInvalidCertificateFails` expects status 400.

Now what about the valid test where PEM is sent with `\\n` escape sequences? Let me trace:
- JSON body: `{"Certificate": "-----BEGIN CERTIFICATE-----\\nMIIB...\\n-----END CERTIFICATE-----\\n"}`
- Jackson parses `\\n` as `\n` (actual newline character)
- Java string: `-----BEGIN CERTIFICATE-----\nMIIB...\n-----END CERTIFICATE-----\n`
- `decodeBlob` sees it starts with `-----BEGIN`, returns as-is
- `parseCertificate` successfully parses the PEM

- `parseCertificate` successfully parses the PEM

- Returns PEM text (starting with `-----BEGIN`) as-is for backward compatibility

    private Response handleImportCertificate(JsonNode request, String region) {
        // AWS JSON 1.1 protocol: Certificate, PrivateKey, and CertificateChain are base64-encoded
        String certificate = decodeBlob(request.path("Certificate").asText(), "Certificate");
        String privateKey = decodeBlob(request.path("PrivateKey").asText(), "PrivateKey");
        String chain = request.path("CertificateChain").asText(null);
        if (chain != null) {
            chain = decodeBlob(chain, "CertificateChain");
        }
        String existingArn = request.path("CertificateArn").asText(null);
        Map<String, String> tags = parseTags(request.path("Tags"));

        Certificate cert = service.importCertificate(certificate, privateKey, chain, existingArn, tags, region);

        ObjectNode response = objectMapper.createObjectNode();
        response.put("CertificateArn", cert.getArn());
        return Response.ok(response).build();
    }

    /**
     * Decodes a base64-encoded blob field, with fallback for plain-text PEM.
     *
     * <p>The AWS JSON 1.1 protocol specifies that binary blob fields (like Certificate,
     * PrivateKey, CertificateChain) are base64-encoded. However, some SDKs or direct HTTP
     * calls may send the raw PEM text. This method detects base64 encoding and decodes
     * accordingly.</p>
     */
    private String decodeBlob(String value, String fieldName) {
        if (value == null || value.isEmpty()) {
            return value;
        }
        // If the value looks like PEM (starts with "-----BEGIN"), it's already plain text
        if (value.startsWith("-----BEGIN")) {
            return value;
        }
        // Otherwise, try to base64-decode it.
        // Use MIME decoder to handle possible whitespace/newlines in the base64 string.
        try {
            byte[] decoded = java.util.Base64.getMimeDecoder().decode(value);
            String result = new String(decoded, java.nio.charset.StandardCharsets.UTF_8);
            // Verify the decoded result is valid PEM text
            if (result.startsWith("-----BEGIN")) {
                return result;
            }
            // If decoded but doesn't look like PEM, return original (might be a different encoding)
            return value;
        } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) {
            // Not valid base64 - return as-is (it might be plain text with escaped newlines)
            return value;
        }
    }

+    /**
+     * Decodes a base64-encoded blob field, with fallback for plain-text PEM.
+     *
+     * <p>The AWS JSON 1.1 protocol specifies that binary blob fields (like Certificate,
+     * PrivateKey, CertificateChain) are base64-encoded. However, some SDKs or direct HTTP
+     * calls may send the raw PEM text. This method detects base64 encoding and decodes
+     * accordingly.</p>
+     */
+    private String decodeBlob(String value, String fieldName) {
+        if (value == null || value.isEmpty()) {
+            return value;
+        }
+        // If the value looks like PEM (starts with "-----BEGIN"), it's already plain text
+        if (value.startsWith("-----BEGIN")) {
+            return value;
+        }
+        // Otherwise, try to base64-decode it.
+        // Use MIME decoder to handle possible whitespace/newlines in the base64 string.
+        try {
+            byte[] decoded = java.util.Base64.getMimeDecoder().decode(value);
+            String result = new String(decoded, java.nio.charset.StandardCharsets.UTF_8);
+            // Verify the decoded result is valid PEM text
+            if (result.startsWith("-----BEGIN")) {
+                return result;
+            }
+            // If decoded but doesn't look like PEM, return original (might be a different encoding)
+            return value;
+        } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) {
+            // Not valid base64 - return as-is (it might be plain text with escaped newlines)
+            return value;
+        }
+    }
